## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / thermo-mechanical behavior of materials
**Analysis**: Task involves stress (sigma) as a function of strain (epsilon) and temperature (T), which is central to material constitutive modeling. The relationship likely captures elastic-plastic deformation with temperature-dependent properties such as thermal softening and thermal expansion effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * epsilon (thermo-elastic behavior where Young's modulus varies linearly with temperature)
- Power-law hardening with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 + c2 * T) (strain hardening exponent with linear thermal effect)
- Exponential thermal activation: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (flow stress with temperature-dependent thermal activation)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Swift hardening law: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (pre-strain power-law hardening)
- Voce hardening law: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon) (saturation stress model, often for alloys)
- Voce law with temperature: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)) * (1 + c3 * T) (saturation stress scaling with temperature)
- Thermal strain correction: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1 * T) (stress from total strain minus linear thermal expansion)
- Ramberg-Osgood approximation: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic plus plastic power-law component)
- Yield with combined hardening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (multiplicative thermal softening on flow stress)
- Bilinear smooth transition: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * (epsilon - c2) * (1 + tanh(c3 * (epsilon - c2))) / 2 (smooth yield onset)
- Modified power-law with temperature shift: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1 * T)**c2 (temperature alters effective strain)
- Linear hardening with quadratic temperature effect: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon) * (1 + c2 * T + c3 * T**2) (polynomial thermal softening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening: stress increases with strain with a concave downward shape (power-law exponent between 0 and 1)
- Thermal softening: stress decreases monotonically as temperature increases, often multiplicatively or via negative exponential
- Yield onset: transition from elastic (linear) to plastic (non-linear) behavior can be modeled by additive combination of linear and power-law terms
- Saturation stress: at large strains stress approaches a constant value, modeled by terms like 1 - exp(-c*epsilon)
- Thermal expansion stress: when total strain includes thermal contribution, stress is proportional to (epsilon - alpha*T), giving negative sensitivity to T
- Flow stress decomposition: multiplicative separation into strain hardening function and thermal softening function, sigma = f(epsilon)*g(T)
- Pre-strain effect: shift in strain reference (epsilon + epsilon_0) accounts for initial residual strains
- Modulus temperature dependence: Young's modulus often decreases linearly with temperature, so first-order term c0*(1 - c1*T)*epsilon
- Work hardening rate: decreasing derivative d(sigma)/d(epsilon) with strain, typical in metals, implying power-law or exponential forms
